## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of state variables x (position) and v (velocity), which is the standard state-space form of a (possibly nonlinear) second-order oscillator. Common models in this domain include nonlinear restoring forces, nonlinear damping, and external/parametric time-dependent forcing via t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator (state form): dv_dt = c0 * x (small-amplitude restoring force; sign absorbed in c0)
- Linear oscillator with viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (mass-spring-damper; c1 typically negative for damping)
- Time-dependent stiffness (parametric oscillator): dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (parametric excitation / Mathieu-type structure)
- Externally forced linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t + c4) (periodic driving force)
- Simple pendulum (nonlinear restoring): dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (large-angle pendulum approximation in state form with damping)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (hardening/softening spring with damping)
- Higher-order odd restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v (polynomial potential expansion for symmetric nonlinear springs)
- Quadratic damping (drag-like): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * Abs(v) (velocity-squared dissipative force)
- Nonlinear damping (velocity-dependent): dv_dt = c0 * x + (c1 + c2 * v**2) * v (Rayleigh-type damping structure)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + (c1 + c2 * x**2) * v (self-excited oscillator; negative damping at small |x|, positive at large |x|)
- LiÃ©nard-type oscillator (general form): dv_dt = c0 * x + (c1 + c2 * x**2 + c3 * x**4) * v (broad class producing limit cycles)
- Conservative nonlinear oscillator from potential gradient: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (no v term; energy-conserving idealization)
- Nonlinear forced Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear resonance/chaos-capable)
- State-dependent frequency shift (amplitude-dependent stiffness): dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * x**2) * x + c2 * v (effective stiffness increases/decreases with amplitude)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative vs dissipative signature: absence of v terms in dv_dt suggests near-conservative dynamics; linear-in-v or nonlinear-in-v terms suggest damping/energy injection.
- Odd symmetry in restoring force: if dv_dt as a function of x is predominantly odd (x, x**3, sin(c*x)), it indicates a symmetric potential about x = 0 (typical for many springs).
- Pendulum-style nonlinearity: sin(c*x) restoring terms indicate angle-based kinematics where torque is proportional to sin(angle), not to angle.
- Amplitude-dependent frequency: inclusion of x**3 or x**5 in restoring force implies frequency shifts with oscillation amplitude (hardening/softening behavior).
- Self-excitation / limit cycles: terms like (c0 + c1 * x**2) * v or (c0 + c1 * v**2) * v can represent negative damping at small amplitude and positive damping at large amplitude, producing stable oscillations.
- Aerodynamic/quadratic drag: v * Abs(v) indicates drag proportional to speed squared (direction opposing velocity), common at higher Reynolds numbers.
- Periodic forcing fingerprint: additive cos(c*t + phase) terms indicate external drives; resonance occurs when forcing frequency is near the oscillatorâ€™s natural frequency.
- Parametric excitation fingerprint: multiplicative modulation (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x indicates time-varying stiffness; instability bands (Mathieu-like) can appear.
- Model identifiability hint: if dv_dt depends strongly on v but weakly on x, dynamics may be dominated by dissipation/actuation; if strongly on x, dominated by restoring force/potential.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO41)

GT: -mu*(c0 - x**c1)*v - omega0**c2*x*exp(-Abs(x))

I need to determine which candidates can match the GT expression:

**GT:** `-0.493165631499977*v*(1 - x**2) - 1.16769962902767*x*exp(-Abs(x))`

Expanding: `0.493165631499977*v*x**2 - 0.493165631499977*v - 1.16769962902767*x*exp(-Abs(x))`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `v*x**2` (coefficient â‰ˆ 0.4932)
2. `v` (coefficient â‰ˆ -0.4932)
3. `x*exp(-Abs(x))` (coefficient â‰ˆ -1.1677)

The key challenge: **`x*exp(-Abs(x))`** is a specific non-polynomial function. The candidates use polynomial and other basis functions. I need to check if any candidate can exactly represent `x*exp(-Abs(x))`.

Note that `x*exp(-Abs(x))` is NOT a polynomial, NOT `x*Abs(x)`, and cannot be exactly represented by polynomials, `sin`, `log`, etc. However, many candidates contain `x*Abs(x)`, polynomial terms in x, and other terms.

Let me think about whether `x*exp(-Abs(x))` can be represented by any combination of the basis functions present in the candidates.

**Key observation:** `x*exp(-Abs(x))` is an odd function that decays exponentially. No finite polynomial can match it exactly. `x*Abs(x)` is odd but grows quadratically. No finite combination of `x`, `x*Abs(x)`, `x**3`, `x**5`, etc. can equal `x*exp(-Abs(x))` for all x.

Let me check special candidates:

- **Candidate 19:** Has `log(c8*exp(c9*x) + 1)` â€” this is a softplus-type function, not equivalent to `x*exp(-Abs(x))`.
- **Candidate 20:** Has `x**2*exp(c9*v)` â€” depends on v exponentially, not matching.
- **Candidate 28:** Has `v*exp(c9*x)` â€” this mixes v with exp(x), can't produce `x*exp(-Abs(x))`.
- **Candidate 36:** Has `x/(c7 + Abs(x))**3` and `v*exp(c9*t)` â€” neither matches.
- **Candidate 43:** Has `x/(c6 + Abs(x))**3` â€” rational in |x|, not exponential.
- **Candidate 47:** Has `x/(c7 + Abs(x))**3` â€” same issue.
- **Candidate 48:** Has `exp(c5*v)` â€” wrong variable.
- **Candidate 44:** Has `exp(c5*t)` â€” wrong variable.
- **Candidate 23:** Has `x/(c9 + Abs(x))**3` â€” rational, not exponential.

None of the candidates contain `exp(-Abs(x))` or any function that could exactly reproduce `x*exp(-Abs(x))`. All candidates are built from polynomials in x, `x*Abs(x)`, `v` terms, and occasionally `sin`, `log`, `cos(t)`, `exp(v)`, `exp(t)`, `exp(x)`, or rational functions of `Abs(x)` â€” none of which can exactly equal `x*exp(-Abs(x))`.

Since `x*exp(-Abs(x))` cannot be exactly represented by any of these basis functions, **no candidate can match the GT**.
